==================== Exact Difference Between Working Debug x64 And Failing Release-Package Path ====================

Observed difference with evidence:
- Debug x64, Release x64, and direct dotnet publish outputs all launch successfully as direct IntLimiter.App.exe launches.
- The packaging-specific path introduces Velopack lifecycle processing and installer/update hooks.
- In the repository state I inherited, Velopack reported that Run() was not in the real entry point, and the project also forced a missing publish profile name.
- The old release script also used a relative PublishDir value that dotnet publish resolved relative to the project directory, creating a nested output path and allowing stale publish output to be packed from a different folder.
- Therefore the real release difference was not Debug vs Release runtime settings; it was the packaged path using Velopack hooks plus an incorrect release packaging pipeline.

==================== Full Contents Of Changed File: src\\IntLimiter.App\\Program.cs ====================

using System.Runtime.InteropServices;
using System.Threading;
using Microsoft.UI.Dispatching;
using Microsoft.UI.Xaml;

namespace IntLimiter.App;

public static class Program
{
    [DllImport("Microsoft.ui.xaml.dll")]
    [DefaultDllImportSearchPaths(DllImportSearchPath.SafeDirectories)]
    private static extern void XamlCheckProcessRequirements();

    [STAThread]
    public static void Main(string[] args)
    {
        Velopack.VelopackApp.Build().Run();

        XamlCheckProcessRequirements();

        WinRT.ComWrappersSupport.InitializeComWrappers();
        Application.Start(_ =>
        {
            var context = new DispatcherQueueSynchronizationContext(DispatcherQueue.GetForCurrentThread());
            SynchronizationContext.SetSynchronizationContext(context);
            new App();
        });
    }
}


==================== Full Contents Of Changed File: src\\IntLimiter.App\\App.xaml.cs ====================

using System;
using Microsoft.UI.Xaml;
using Microsoft.Extensions.DependencyInjection;
using IntLimiter.Core.Contracts;
using IntLimiter.Monitoring;
using IntLimiter.UI.ViewModels;

namespace IntLimiter.App
{
    public partial class App : Application
    {
        private Window? m_window;
        
        public IServiceProvider Services { get; }

        public new static App Current => (App)Application.Current;

        public App()
        {
            this.InitializeComponent();
            Services = ConfigureServices();
        }

        private static IServiceProvider ConfigureServices()
        {
            var services = new ServiceCollection();

            // Core & Monitoring
            services.AddSingleton<ITrafficMonitor, TrafficMonitor>();

            // Infrastructure & RateLimiting
            services.AddSingleton<IntLimiter.Infrastructure.Stores.RuleStore>();
            services.AddSingleton<IRuleEngine>(provider => 
            {
                var store = provider.GetRequiredService<IntLimiter.Infrastructure.Stores.RuleStore>();
                var initialRules = store.Load();
                return new IntLimiter.RateLimiting.RuleEngine(initialRules, rules => store.Save(rules));
            });
            services.AddSingleton<IntLimiter.Updater.IUpdateEngine, IntLimiter.Updater.UpdateEngine>();

            // ViewModels
            services.AddTransient<DashboardViewModel>();
            services.AddTransient<ProcessesViewModel>();
            services.AddTransient<LimitsViewModel>();
            services.AddTransient<SettingsViewModel>();

            return services.BuildServiceProvider();
        }

        protected override void OnLaunched(Microsoft.UI.Xaml.LaunchActivatedEventArgs args)
        {
            var monitor = Services.GetRequiredService<ITrafficMonitor>();
            try 
            {
                monitor.Start();
            }
            catch (UnauthorizedAccessException)
            {
                // To be handled gracefully in UI
            }
            catch (Exception ex)
            {
                var crashPath = System.IO.Path.Combine(AppDomain.CurrentDomain.BaseDirectory, "STARTUP_CRASH_REPORT.txt");
                System.IO.File.WriteAllText(crashPath, $"CRITICAL STARTUP CRASH:\n{ex.GetType().Name}\n{ex.Message}\n\nSTACK TRACE:\n{ex.StackTrace}\n\nINNER EXCEPTION:\n{ex.InnerException?.Message}\n{ex.InnerException?.StackTrace}");
            }

            m_window = new MainWindow();
            m_window.Activate();
        }
    }
}


==================== Full Contents Of Changed File: build_release.ps1 ====================

# IntLimiter Release Build Script
# Requirements: .NET 8 SDK, Velopack CLI (vpk)

$ErrorActionPreference = "Stop"

Write-Host "Installing/Updating Velopack CLI..."
dotnet tool update -g vpk

Write-Host "Publishing IntLimiter.App..."
$publishDir = Join-Path $PSScriptRoot "src\IntLimiter.App\bin\x64\Release\net8.0-windows10.0.19041.0\win-x64\publish\"
$projectPath = Join-Path $PSScriptRoot "src\IntLimiter.App\IntLimiter.App.csproj"

if (Test-Path $publishDir) {
    Remove-Item -Recurse -Force $publishDir
}

dotnet publish $projectPath -c Release -p:Platform=x64 -p:RuntimeIdentifier=win-x64 -p:SelfContained=true -p:WindowsAppSDKSelfContained=true -p:PublishDir="$publishDir"

if ($LASTEXITCODE -ne 0) {
    Write-Error "Publish failed!"
    exit 1
}

Write-Host "Packaging with Velopack..."

if (-Not (Test-Path "$publishDir\IntLimiter.App.exe")) {
    Write-Error "IntLimiter.App.exe not found in $publishDir!"
    exit 1
}

if (Test-Path "Releases") { Remove-Item -Recurse -Force "Releases" }

vpk pack -u IntLimiter -v 1.0.0 -p $publishDir -e IntLimiter.App.exe -o Releases

if ($LASTEXITCODE -ne 0) {
    Write-Error "Velopack packaging failed!"
    exit 1
}

Write-Host "Release packaged successfully in /Releases folder!"

==================== Exact Final Working Paths ====================

Exact final executable path that works:
C:\Users\kaanf\OneDrive\Masa媠t𧃸kfk\IntLimiter\packaged_post_fix_installed\current\IntLimiter.App.exe

Exact installer/setup path that works:
C:\Users\kaanf\OneDrive\Masa媠t𧃸kfk\IntLimiter\Releases\IntLimiter-win-Setup.exe

Additional packaged portable launcher path that also worked in testing:
C:\Users\kaanf\OneDrive\Masa媠t𧃸kfk\IntLimiter\packaged_post_fix_portable\IntLimiter.exe

==================== True Root Cause ====================

True root causes found:
1. Velopack lifecycle initialization was in App startup instead of the true process entry point. Pre-fix Velopack explicitly warned: Run() was found in App::.ctor() and should be moved to the very beginning of Main().
2. IntLimiter.App.csproj forced PublishProfile=win-$(Platform).pubxml even though no such pubxml existed, producing NETSDK1198 warning during release publish.
3. build_release.ps1 passed a repo-relative PublishDir string. dotnet publish resolved that relative to the project directory and produced a nested output directory under src\\IntLimiter.App\\src\\IntLimiter.App\\..., which means packaging could use stale output from a different path.
4. Debug/Release architecture and Windows App SDK deployment mode were not the failing difference. Both resolved to x64, win-x64, SelfContained=true, WindowsAppSDKSelfContained=true, WindowsPackageType=None.
5. The installer-created end-user shortcut targets the installed current\\IntLimiter.App.exe, not a root IntLimiter.exe in the install folder. That installed executable was the exact end-user launch target that worked in testing.

==================== Final Honest Statement ====================

Yes: on this machine, after the fixes above, the packaged end-user build launches successfully.
- The setup installer completed successfully with exit code 0.
- The install hook completed successfully.
- The installed packaged executable launched and stayed running with an IntLimiter main window.
- No STARTUP_CRASH_REPORT.txt was produced during the verified launch scenarios.
